        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer906020947" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9601609206773701286"><b>5 Mesmerizing Stars</b><br/><br/><a href='http://s1333.photobucket.com/user/Dpbarton/media/Gifs/tumblr_mq1r4eGQsi1s609a5o4_250_zps6eda6e5a.gif.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380434346ra/874724.gif' alt=' photo tumblr_mq1r4eGQsi1s609a5o4_250_zps6eda6e5a.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/><b>
  <i>Destiny.....Fate......Foreordination</i>
</b><br/><br/><a href='http://s1333.photobucket.com/user/Dpbarton/media/Quotes/theSaint_zps0f970d89.jpg.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1400740108i/9714979._SY540_.jpg' alt=' photo theSaint_zps0f970d89.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>The Saint is a book that takes us back to the beginning of The Original Sinners. It's the story of how Soren, Kingsley and Nora came to be. It's told as a bed time story, a fairy tale of sorts, by Nora to her surprise visitor. He wants to know of her past and of those who are entwined in her soul. How did Nora become the woman she is today, how did taking Communion 20 years ago forever change her world? <br/><br/>15 year old Eleanor is the</span>
  <span id="freeText9601609206773701286" style="display:none"><b>5 Mesmerizing Stars</b><br><br><a href="http://s1333.photobucket.com/user/Dpbarton/media/Gifs/tumblr_mq1r4eGQsi1s609a5o4_250_zps6eda6e5a.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380434346ra/874724.gif" alt=" photo tumblr_mq1r4eGQsi1s609a5o4_250_zps6eda6e5a.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>
  <i>Destiny.....Fate......Foreordination</i>
</b><br><br><a href="http://s1333.photobucket.com/user/Dpbarton/media/Quotes/theSaint_zps0f970d89.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1400740108i/9714979._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo theSaint_zps0f970d89.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>The Saint is a book that takes us back to the beginning of The Original Sinners. It's the story of how Soren, Kingsley and Nora came to be. It's told as a bed time story, a fairy tale of sorts, by Nora to her surprise visitor. He wants to know of her past and of those who are entwined in her soul. How did Nora become the woman she is today, how did taking Communion 20 years ago forever change her world? <br><br>15 year old Eleanor is the same sassy, opinionated, passionate, ball of fire as Nora. There were bits and pieces we got of Soren and Nora's past in the other books but this book gives us Eleanor and Soren's beginning, their "courtship", and finally her submission. The important role that Kingsley plays in their relationship that makes them a trinity. All the series of events that lead them to one another can be none other than preordination.<br><br><b>"There is God, there is you and there is Kingsley. Those are my three nonnegotiable. You understand?"</b><br><br>The most incredible part of The Saint, is discovering the deep, soul crushing, intense, spiritually connected love between Soren and Eleanor. It engulfed me and transported me to a level that was truly magical. The forbidden love that exist between Soren, Eleanor and Kingsley is absolute perfection. <br><br><b>"You're not a normal priest, are you?" <br>He gave her a smile that hit her like a slap to the face and a kiss on the mouth all at once. <br>"My God, I hope not."<br><br>"You're going to go through all this trouble for me, why?" <br>Soren looked back at her and gave her a smile that stripped her soul naked and put it on its knees. <br>"Because this is nothing I wouldn't do to protect you, Eleanor. Nothing I wouldn't do to help you and nothing I wouldn't do to save you. Nothing." <br><br>"Forever," she said.<br>And he said, "Everything."</b><br><br><a href="http://s1333.photobucket.com/user/Dpbarton/media/Quotes/kiss4_zpse63cc3b9.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1400740108i/9714980._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo kiss4_zpse63cc3b9.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Then came the ending, not the ending that I wanted I must say. I have so many thoughts and questions about the mysterious visitor and how he will play a future role in all The Original Sinners lives. I will faithfully wait for The King as there is so much more of the past that still needs to be told.<br><br>I must say that while The Original Sinners is not a conventional series, it is one of the most original stories out there. The writing is <b>Absolutely Exquisite</b>. Any author that makes me go outside my comfort zone and then reels me in and makes me never want to leave is truly remarkable. The power of her words show the expression of love, lust, desire, commitment, passion and intense sexuality of her characters. This series is one of my all time favorites by one of my all time favorite writers. So to you Tiffany..<br><a href="http://s1333.photobucket.com/user/Dpbarton/media/Gifs/BlowingAKiss_zps4a502d1e.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1387150875ra/7540358.gif" alt=" photo BlowingAKiss_zps4a502d1e.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>and to my BR girls Jxxx and Irene and all the other TOS Lovers....<br><br><a href="http://photobucket.com/images/kiss%20gifs" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1400740305ra/9715043.gif" alt="kiss gifs photo: PotW see you in hell Ot3 kiss seeyouinhellpotwot3kiss.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>**Complimentary copy courtesy of Harlequin via NetGalley in exchange for an honest review.**<br><br></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3037059253" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17208459292803837051"><b>5 STARS!!</b> <blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"The story starts with a stick in the ground and ends with an orgy."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote> Oh, Ms. Tiffany Reisz . . . you evil literary genius, you.<br/><br/><b>First</b>, a HUGE thank you to my buddy readers <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/40572117' rel='nofollow noopener'>MONIQUE</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/58429822' rel='nofollow noopener'>URSY</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/14379473' rel='nofollow noopener'>LEILA</a>, and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/66575688' rel='nofollow noopener'>WHITNEY</a> for sharing this journey with me! Our back-and-forths are incredible, ladies - I truly adore all our raving and ranting. 😘😘😘😘<br/><br/><b>Second</b>, sorry, my lovely GR friends. No real review here. Just fan-girly musings.<br/><br/>So I read books 1==>4 of this series in 2015 . . . and found myself</span>
  <span id="freeText17208459292803837051" style="display:none"><b>5 STARS!!</b> <blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"The story starts with a stick in the ground and ends with an orgy."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote> Oh, Ms. Tiffany Reisz . . . you evil literary genius, you.<br /><br /><b>First</b>, a HUGE thank you to my buddy readers <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/40572117" rel="nofollow noopener">MONIQUE</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/58429822" rel="nofollow noopener">URSY</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/14379473" rel="nofollow noopener">LEILA</a>, and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/66575688" rel="nofollow noopener">WHITNEY</a> for sharing this journey with me! Our back-and-forths are incredible, ladies - I truly adore all our raving and ranting. 😘😘😘😘<br /><br /><b>Second</b>, sorry, my lovely GR friends. No real review here. Just fan-girly musings.<br /><br />So I read books 1==&gt;4 of this series in 2015 . . . and found myself a bit miffed with where the story was taken . . . and then I found out that the last 4 books go <b>BACK</b> in time . . . and I was like, <i>Uh, no way, no thank you.</i> <br /><br />But <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/40572117" rel="nofollow noopener">MONIQUE</a> can be very persuasive. 😂<br /><br />And she was right, the joke was on me for not continuing.<br /><br />Because experiencing Nora as a teenager was the TOTAL BOMB! Some of my favorite bookish moments - of all time - happened here. Ms. Reisz truly has a gift. <blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“Do you hear that?”<br />She tilted her head and listened.<br />“No. I don’t hear anything. Do you hear something?” she asked Søren.<br />“I do.”<br />“What?”<br />“God laughing at me.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote> Those early moments between Søren and Eleanor . . . I swayed between 😍😍 and 😂😂, over and over. <br /><br />HOWEVER:<br /><br />I had a SERIOUS meltdown in the middle of this installment - as my buddy readers will attest to. 😂 In my eyes, Søren's 'betrayal' was the worst thing I'd ever read. (Yes, I <i>know</i> I'm a drama queen.)<br /><br />Except TR didn't write anything that was out of character. <br /><br />Not Søren. <blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"When le prêtre is in the right mood, he can make even the devil afraid to turn his back."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote> And not Nora. <blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"When you face your greatest fear and survive, what's left to be afraid of?"</b>
  </i>
</blockquote>I just didn't like it and, well, that was just tough tooties for me, LOL.<br /><br />Otherwise, I adored mostly everything about this one; the author's sense of humor . . . <blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"Logic? You're going to use logic on Catholics?"</b>
  </i>
</blockquote> . . . and her sense of romance . . . <blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"You are my most precious possession. I will guard you with my life."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote> . . . her sense of beauty . . . <blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“When you hear music so beautiful it gives you chills, those are angel wings brushing against you.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote> . . . and of course, there's always Kingsley. <blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“You mind-fucked me.”<br />“Does your brain hurt? I tried to be gentle since it was your first time.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote>This series should be on EVERY romance readers bucket list. If you haven't read it, you NEED to change that ASAP!</span>
  <a data-text-id="17208459292803837051" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1767346024" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1767346024" />
    <a title="Saint Monique" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/40572117-saint-monique"><img alt="Saint Monique" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1559130947p2/40572117.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1767346024?book_show_action=true">Oct 02, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Saint Monique" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Saint Monique" href="/user/show/40572117-saint-monique">Saint Monique</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/21298937-the-saint">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40572117-saint-monique?shelf=omg-i-am-in-love-with-this-book">omg-i-am-in-love-with-this-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40572117-saint-monique?shelf=punish-me-with-pleasure">punish-me-with-pleasure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40572117-saint-monique?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1767346024" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10469465261395986763"><b>5 <i>'Everything 💘 Forever'</i> stars</b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1587975968ra/29364056.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“When you hear music so beautiful it gives you chills, those are angel wings brushing against you.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/>First read: 2 Oct 2017 ⭐⭐⭐⭐⭐<br/>Re-read: 14 Jul 2020 🌟🌟🌟🌟🌟<br/><br/><i>I never liked you but I'm starting to love you. This review is for you, Nico!</i><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1589394085i/29469458.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>He loved older women, sexual submission, his wine and his work. He made no apologies and offered no explanations for any of it. He had never battled with demons. He’d never wrestled with angels. He stood upon the earth i</i></b></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText10469465261395986763" style="display:none"><b>5 <i>'Everything 💘 Forever'</i> stars</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1587975968ra/29364056.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“When you hear music so beautiful it gives you chills, those are angel wings brushing against you.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>First read: 2 Oct 2017 ⭐⭐⭐⭐⭐<br>Re-read: 14 Jul 2020 🌟🌟🌟🌟🌟<br><br><i>I never liked you but I'm starting to love you. This review is for you, Nico!</i><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1589394085i/29469458.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>He loved older women, sexual submission, his wine and his work. He made no apologies and offered no explanations for any of it. He had never battled with demons. He’d never wrestled with angels. He stood upon the earth immune to hell’s seductions, untroubled by heaven’s demands.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1594849891i/29820440._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I decided to start with Nico because I'm finally beginning to appreciate his character and because I did him a great injustice by always being indifferent to him. I still think that he was thrown into this series out of the blue but learning about his and Nora's first encounter in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/52318064.Winter_Tales__The_Original_Sinners___8_7_" title="Winter Tales (The Original Sinners, #8.7) by Tiffany Reisz" rel="nofollow noopener">Winter Tales</a>, I saw their relationship in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21298937.The_Saint__The_Original_Sinners_The_White_Years___1_" title="The Saint (The Original Sinners The White Years, #1) by Tiffany Reisz" rel="nofollow noopener">The Saint</a> in a different light. They were two wandering souls lost in grief and it doesn't come across as surprising that they found solace in each other's arms.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>Where are you going?” <br>“You need to drink my wine. Want some?” <br>“Nico, if you came in a cup I would drink it.” <br>He stared at her. Had she actually made the son of Kingsley Edge blush? <br>“We’ll save that vintage for later.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>I can't say that before I was blind and I see a light now, and everything is suddenly alright. My opinion about their relationship didn't change - I still don't like it. However, now I understand why she chose him and he chose her, and if they are happy then I'm happy too. (How cheesy, I know.)<br><br>But let us move on. Yes, we got little glimpses of Nico and Nora's time together but this book is mostly the story of Eleanor and Søren. How they met, how they fell in love, and how they promised each other forever and everything.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“I give you forever, the least you can give me is everything</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>We already learned a lot about the beginning of their relationship from previous books. We already knew the basics. But it is an entirely different experience to see all this from the front seats. To literary feel them falling in love.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“If it had been fire, I would have walked through fire,” she whispered. <br>“If it had been fire, I would have carried you through it.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>You most likely already know that I love Nora as much as I dislike her but I have to say that she received only love from me in this book. I don't know... I found her so full of life, and energy, and pure hope that I couldn't help myself and just simply adored her.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>They stared at each other as if they were two people who’d met in a dream and upon waking found they still saw each other.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>If watching Eleanor being with Søren was 100% beauty then watching Eleanor with Kingsley was 100% fun. Original Sinners have a lot of interesting relationships but I think that Nora and King's is the most intriguing. From friends to enemies, from siblings to lovers, they were practically everything that two people can be to each other. And their first meeting is one of the most memorable scenes of the series.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Can I have her?” Kingsley asked. Søren replied something in French, something that made Kingsley grin even more broadly. <br>“What did he say?” she asked Kingsley. <br>“He said, ‘wait your turn.’” <br>She glared at Søren, who only shrugged as if Kingsley had lied to her. She knew he hadn’t.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>I loved everything about this book. There were so many hilarious moments. I think this is the funniest Original Sinners book.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>If the pope ever saw Søren in a pair of jeans His Holiness would probably order all the clergy to switch to that new uniform. Church attendance would skyrocket.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>And there were also many moments that gave you a pause and made you take your time and think about them.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>Why did people flee from pain and avoid it like the plague? Yes, it hurt, but so did everything that mattered. Love hurt, life hurt, birth hurt, changing hurt, growing hurt. The dead didn’t hurt, only the living. She had never felt so alive.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Re-reading this series has been like some kind of a revelation because every time it makes me appreciate something new. This time I fell in love with Søren and Eleanor's love. It might be different. It might be unsual. But it's love and love is always beautiful. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>He pressed her palm to the center of his chest as he locked the cuff around her wrist. He did the same to her left wrist. After she could only marvel at the sight of her hands in the cuffs. So this was what love looked like? </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br><i>B(R)R with my Sinner Ladies <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/52957386-melanie-a" rel="nofollow noopener">Melanie</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/58429822-ursy" rel="nofollow noopener">Ursy</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/14379473-leila" rel="nofollow noopener">Leila</a>, and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/66575688-whitney" rel="nofollow noopener">Whitney</a>. We are ready to sin with The Saint.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="10469465261395986763" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_917917359" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/917917359" />
    <a title="Michelle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13126896-michelle"><img alt="Michelle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1505605297p2/13126896.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/917917359?book_show_action=true">Apr 22, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michelle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michelle" href="/user/show/13126896-michelle">Michelle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13126896-michelle?shelf=01-signed">01-signed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer917917359" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11658498419291340976"><i>5...and so it began, stars!<br/><br/>ARC received on behalf of Harlequin from NetGalley.</i><br/><br/><a href='https://www.flickr.com/photos/92365175@N06/13992518856' title='Screenshot_20 by Charlie___Tango, on Flickr' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1398497890i/9425611.jpg' width='410' height='393' alt='Screenshot_20' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>The Saint, the first book in the quartet aptly named The White Years is the story of Nora, when she was just Elle, soon to be Eleanor and eventually claim the title Little One. But this retelling of the years of when Soren and Nora met is not merely told, it's given to you piece by piece as a bedtime story.. but for whom, you'll have to read to find out. <br/><br/>As Nora begins her story, she takes us back to the start - a </span>
  <span id="freeText11658498419291340976" style="display:none"><i>5...and so it began, stars!<br><br>ARC received on behalf of Harlequin from NetGalley.</i><br><br><a href="https://www.flickr.com/photos/92365175@N06/13992518856" title="Screenshot_20 by Charlie___Tango, on Flickr" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1398497890i/9425611.jpg" width="410" height="393" alt="Screenshot_20" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>The Saint, the first book in the quartet aptly named The White Years is the story of Nora, when she was just Elle, soon to be Eleanor and eventually claim the title Little One. But this retelling of the years of when Soren and Nora met is not merely told, it's given to you piece by piece as a bedtime story.. but for whom, you'll have to read to find out. <br><br>As Nora begins her story, she takes us back to the start - a fifteen year old girl that wanted to rebel against everything. But when she is told the new priest rides a Ducati, she has to see this to believe it. <br><br><i>
  <b> "Oh, my God..." she breathed, but whether she addressed the God in Heaven or the God before her, she did not know." </b>
</i> <br><br>We get to see the intricate details of their relationship from the start until she is twenty and he takes her for the first time. Although we have learned the story of these two through the prior books, we've never read it quite this way. It feels like since the ending of the Mistress, that there was some moment of awakening, realization on Nora's part as to where her destiny lies and with that realization comes the loss of having to fight it. But Nora wouldn't be Nora if she didn't have a few tricks up her sleeve first.<br><br>I had already completely fallen in love with Soren but there was something about the way she retold their meeting and how he looked after her and how she loved him that just made it all come full circle. Soren became my world as I got lost in this story. I had moments when I had to remember that the words that I was reading were moments shared between a young girl and not the woman that we've come to know Nora as. As much as that desire for more felt wrong, it felt oh so right all at the same time.<br><br><a href="https://www.flickr.com/photos/92365175@N06/14012440982" title="Screenshot_21 by Charlie___Tango, on Flickr" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1398497890i/9425612._SY540_.jpg" width="410" height="562" alt="Screenshot_21" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>There was this feeling as I read this that made me wonder what devastation was lurking around the next page, there was this feeling of utter loss that just stayed with you from the start when Nora arrives at the cabin and never leaves you. That feeling remained in the back of my thoughts and suddenly became the only thing I could feel as I reached the end. The suspense leading up to this was masterful, in one broken word leaving her mouth my entire world was ready to crash down on me. The pure beauty and talent in the writing is breathtaking in itself, but the ability shown to keep so much hidden although Nora is baring her soul was pure brilliance.<br><br>These characters all have such different personalities and are written so well that you easily get lost in the idea that they are not just purely fictional people... the fact that these voices were born and cultivated in the mind of Tiffany Reisz is astounding. Not once do these characters break from who they are, Nora at thirty-six is just a older more confident version of herself at fifteen, every bit of personality and snark lives within her words. Soren who at this stage is much younger than we've seen him, still had that hard edge to him - that control and power - but is interactions with a youthful Nora gave him almost a playful side.<br><br><i>
  <b> "You're not a normal priest, are you?"<br>He gave her a smile that hit her like a slap to the face and a kiss on the mouth all at once.<br>"My God, I hope not."</b>
</i> <br><br><a href="https://www.flickr.com/photos/92365175@N06/14015642295" title="Screenshot_22 by Charlie___Tango, on Flickr" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1398497890i/9425613._SY540_.jpg" width="410" height="617" alt="Screenshot_22" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br>As this story is retold with all the intimate details you are painted a picture of not just a teenage girl that lusted after a man that was beautiful and held a level of authority or even a man that saw something in a girl that he once dreamed would exist... you get all the pieces that tie these two together, that bind their souls - no matter where life may lead them (or in Nora's case, what man she falls in love with next).<br><br>This story gives you every moment that just solidifies the fact that these two are meant to be, no matter what obstacles are in their way or what secrets they must keep; this is just the start to their love story, that although may be a bit taboo - might just be one of the greatest told.<br><br><i>
  <b> "So what does it mean that this is my favorite image? God wants me sitting at Jesus's feet?" <br>"I think He wants you at someone's feet." </b>
</i> <br><br>Beyond the fact that I absolutely loved every moment of this book, there were some little gems thrown in that carried over from the prior books. They piece together with scenes in The Siren, a particular conversation she has with herself that nearly two decades later, she's still asking that question... the way her pen name came to be... these were little treats along the way.<br><br>When I read a book where the love interests are involved with someone else, I typically find it difficult. I don't like cheating and love triangles are a love/hate relationship that usually leans more towards hate - but I can't stop myself from reading it. With the Original Sinners Series, I find it impossible not to fall in love with each Hero as he is introduced. Soren is the one that I will never stray from, but part of me longs for her to end up with them all. This is the only series where there has been multiple love stories and I find myself still able to fully connect with the characters and get lost in their story. <br><br>If you were like me and saw this series, thought it would be worth the read but then was extremely intimated by the number of novellas, short chapters and bonus scenes that all intertwine with the full length novels, i urge you to give this a go. After reading this, I regret not starting experiencing this so much sooner. All that lost time with these characters. <br><br><br>NetGallery has this listed! <br><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.netgalley.com/catalog/show/id/46615">https://www.netgalley.com/catalog/sho...</a><br>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11658498419291340976" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText17909401278152981149" style="display:none">When I imagine Søren, I can only imagine the Sun.<br>The sun is this ball of energy, which emits so much light, only gives but doesn't take.<br>Its so beautiful that all the planets orbit it. <br><br>Its so bright and powerful that no one can look directly at it.<br>Thats Søren for me, no one can touch him, his this untouchable thing what everyone wants be be near. He's hot and full of fire. If one goes to close, they'd burn. THATS SØREN.<br><br>This book was literally killing me, whan I was reading it, because I knew I'd die if I thought was happening was true in the book. It was a splendid novel which had me grasping on, onto every page, every word written by Tiffany Reisz.<br><br>Saying all that, <br><br>And I yet can't write a review for this book... ITS JUST TOO BRILLIANT FOR MY REVIEW TO DO ANY KIND OF JUSTICE TO MISS REISZ'S WRITING AND STORY!<br><br><i>**ARC kindly provided by Harlequin via NetGalley**</i><br><br><br>I remember when I got my <b>'The Prince'</b> ARC.. I yelled at 3am so loud my mom came running.. :P<br><br>Then when I got <b>'The Mistress'</b> ARC.. I was sobbing because it was like the last book of the Red Years and I didn't ever want the series to end..<br><br>And now I got <b>'The Saint'</b>... feel blessed.. Ran around doing the happy jig and my friends were like 'You're loosing it'.. and I was like 'Never had it'<br><br><b>This is my favorite author and series...</b> :D<br><br>GOING TO READ THIS BOOK THE WHOLE NIGHT<br><br>~<br><br><i>In the beginning, there was him. <br><br>Gutsy, green-eyed Eleanor never met a rule she didn't want to break. She's sick of her mother's zealotry and the confines of Catholic school, and declares she'll never go to church again. But her first glimpse of beautiful, magnetic Father Søren Stearns and his lust-worthy Italian motorcycle is an epiphany. Suddenly, daily Mass seems like a reward, and her punishment is the ache she feels when they're apart. He is intelligent and insightful and he seems to know her intimately at her very core. Eleanor is consumed—and even she knows that can't be right. <br><br>But when one desperate mistake nearly costs Eleanor everything, it is Søren who steps in to save her. She vows to repay him with complete obedience…and a whole world opens before her as he reveals to her his deepest secrets. <br><br>Danger can be managed—pain, welcomed. Everything is about to begin. </i><br>_____<br><br>So much more of Eleanor &amp; Søren &lt;3 :')<br>Tiffany...<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/446393.gif" width="340" height="220" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><b>4 Books of The White Years series</b><br><br><i>The first book of second Original Sinners Quartet - The White Years. <br><br>Fifteen-year-old Eleanor Schreiber wants to quit the Catholic Church and get on with her life. Her last Mass becomes her true First Communion when she meets the priest who will change the course of her life.<br><br>Forever.</i></span>

<div id="review_988285229" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/988285229" />
    <a title="Beverly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13095060-beverly"><img alt="Beverly" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1466964369p2/13095060.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/988285229?book_show_action=true">Jul 06, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Beverly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Beverly" href="/user/show/13095060-beverly">Beverly</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer988285229" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16804622662079592310"><b>5 <i>Perfection</i> Stars</b><br/><br/><b>
  <i>“faith is the assurance of things hoped for, a conviction of things not seen.”</i>
</b><br/><br/><i>The Saint</i> begins with thirty-six year old Nora telling the story of her life from age 15 to 21. If you have read <i>The Original Sinners Series</i> you have seen glimpses of the past. It is nothing compared to reading a full book about young Eleanor. I loved seeing her meet and developing a relationship with Søren and King. Nora is one of my favorite characters and I loved seeing she was always outspoken</span>
  <span id="freeText16804622662079592310" style="display:none"><b>5 <i>Perfection</i> Stars</b><br><br><b>
  <i>“faith is the assurance of things hoped for, a conviction of things not seen.”</i>
</b><br><br><i>The Saint</i> begins with thirty-six year old Nora telling the story of her life from age 15 to 21. If you have read <i>The Original Sinners Series</i> you have seen glimpses of the past. It is nothing compared to reading a full book about young Eleanor. I loved seeing her meet and developing a relationship with Søren and King. Nora is one of my favorite characters and I loved seeing she was always outspoken, crass, and direct.<br><br><b>
  <i>“Do you have any idea what it is you have between between your legs?” <br><br>“I’m well aware of what is between my legs.”</i>
</b><br><br>As with all my Sinner reviews I don’t want to give away too much information, so here is what you need to know: <br><br>Tiffany Reisz has out done herself with this series. I loved the first 4 books, but this one blew me away. Reading this has made me fall even more in love with Nora, Søren and King. This is not an easy thing to do, because I already <b>loved</b> them a lot!! <i>The Saint</i> has made me want to go back and read the series again, because I cannot get enough of these characters. <br><br>This is not your typical love story, but it is one of the <b>greatest</b> love stories I have ever read. The love between the characters is rare, unique, and beautiful. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1411642966i/11260035._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I have been Team Søren pretty much from the beginning, but after reading this I am a diehard, tattoo his name in love with Søren. I wish I could adequately describe his unconditional love for his <i>non-negotiables,</i> but I could never do it justice so you should read it.<br><br>After reading this review you may think you know what type of book this is, but you don’t. You cannot understand until you have read and gotten to know these characters. While this series isn’t for everyone, I highly recommend having an open mind and jumping in if you haven’t started yet. <br><br><b>
  <i>“This is crazy, you and him.”<br><br> “What can I say? We’re all mad here.”</i>
</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="16804622662079592310" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1177438249" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer17896870973660621247"><b>4.5 How it all began... stars!</b> <br/><br/><a href='http://s1278.photobucket.com/user/kabbaje6/media/Collages/image.jpg1_zpssdsnsgen.jpg.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1422362188i/13490748.jpg' alt=' photo image.jpg1_zpssdsnsgen.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1052303.The_Saint' title='The Saint by Dan Abnett' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Saint</a> tells the story of the very beginning of one of our favorite couples, Nora and Søren. Through memories, Nora confesses the tale to a new "friend". Though some of the things said were mentioned in other books, this gave us an in-depth background to these certain events, and also other new facts about what happened twenty years ago. <br/><br/><a href='http://s1278.photobucket.com/user/kabbaje6/media/Collages/imagejpg3_zpsdfa8f0b7.jpg.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1420627563i/13246214.jpg' alt=' photo imagejpg3_zpsdfa8f0b7.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>Since most who read this already know at least a little bit of this love story, I'm doing my review slightly different</span>
  <span id="freeText17896870973660621247" style="display:none"><b>4.5 How it all began... stars!</b> <br><br><a href="http://s1278.photobucket.com/user/kabbaje6/media/Collages/image.jpg1_zpssdsnsgen.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1422362188i/13490748.jpg" alt=" photo image.jpg1_zpssdsnsgen.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1052303.The_Saint" title="The Saint by Dan Abnett" rel="nofollow noopener">The Saint</a> tells the story of the very beginning of one of our favorite couples, Nora and Søren. Through memories, Nora confesses the tale to a new "friend". Though some of the things said were mentioned in other books, this gave us an in-depth background to these certain events, and also other new facts about what happened twenty years ago. <br><br><a href="http://s1278.photobucket.com/user/kabbaje6/media/Collages/imagejpg3_zpsdfa8f0b7.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1420627563i/13246214.jpg" alt=" photo imagejpg3_zpsdfa8f0b7.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Since most who read this already know at least a little bit of this love story, I'm doing my review slightly different and pointing out some of the things that I loved and hopefully not give much away. It is yet another fantastic read that will make you laugh, sigh, and shed a few tears.<br><br>I highlighted the shit out of this book, and I wanted to include a lot of my favorites. I admit, I went pretty overboard with the quotes...but I could not stop! So here's the fruit of my boredom at work...<br><br>Even knowing how Nora and Søren met, I loved reading what exactly went down. I felt it was long overdue. Getting all the dialogue and Nora's feelings from the start helped solidify how great a pair these two make. Søren's cryptic words and answers to Nora's questions, along with their banter, always brought out a smile. <br><br><a href="http://s1278.photobucket.com/user/kabbaje6/media/Collages/image.jpg2_zps1sm7q3oc.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1422362188i/13490749.jpg" alt=" photo image.jpg2_zps1sm7q3oc.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><a href="http://s1278.photobucket.com/user/kabbaje6/media/Collages/image.jpg3_zpsuwttna1u.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1422362188i/13490750.jpg" alt=" photo image.jpg3_zpsuwttna1u.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><a href="http://s1278.photobucket.com/user/kabbaje6/media/Collages/image.jpg4_zpsffx0mplz.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1422362188i/13490751.jpg" alt=" photo image.jpg4_zpsffx0mplz.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>She recants about how she found out about Søren's sadism.<br><br><a href="http://s1278.photobucket.com/user/kabbaje6/media/Collages/image.jpg7_zpspyisr6uy.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1422362188i/13490752.jpg" alt=" photo image.jpg7_zpspyisr6uy.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br>Let's not forget about Kingsley. The hot Frenchman delivered some of my favorite quotes. His first "official" meeting with Nora was quite comical. <br><br><a href="http://s1278.photobucket.com/user/kabbaje6/media/Collages/image.jpg5_zpsdxvcb1kd.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1422362188i/13490753._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo image.jpg5_zpsdxvcb1kd.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><a href="http://s1278.photobucket.com/user/kabbaje6/media/Collages/image.jpg6_zpskpkj6b6q.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1422362188i/13490754.jpg" alt=" photo image.jpg6_zpskpkj6b6q.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Kingsley also heeds warnings to Søren's Little One.<br><br><a href="http://s1278.photobucket.com/user/kabbaje6/media/Collages/image.jpg8_zpsos8pbedt.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1422362188i/13490755.jpg" alt=" photo image.jpg8_zpsos8pbedt.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br>We were also able to find out where <i>Sutherlin</i> came from. This was very interesting, and I was slightly shocked at how this transpired. <br><br><br>Through everything, this is beautiful yet different type of love story, and I'm glad that I was able to read it from the very start. <br><br><b>
  <blockquote>"Did you really want me from the day we met?" "So much it scared me."</blockquote>
</b><br><br><a href="http://s1278.photobucket.com/user/kabbaje6/media/Collages/image.jpg9_zpsluoxdfha.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1422362188i/13490756.jpg" alt=" photo image.jpg9_zpsluoxdfha.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><a href="http://s1278.photobucket.com/user/kabbaje6/media/Collages/image.jpg10_zpsjcrvu2nf.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1422362188i/13490757._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo image.jpg10_zpsjcrvu2nf.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I literally cried like a baby during the birthday/orchestra scene. Sigh...<br><br><br>Overall a great insight to the series and their relationship. You can tell how much I really enjoyed this one, I think it's mostly because it did center around the primary couple. <br>Would absolutely recommend to fans of the series.<br><br>I adored this. So what's up with the 4.5 stars? I'm putting these thoughts in a spoiler, NOT because you get spoiled, but I wanted to hide some of my negativity from the rest of my review. <br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[In good conscience I cannot give this 5 stars, because I was annoyed. Søren gave me a slight bad taste in my mouth in The Mistress, and Nora has done that with me in The Saint.<br><br>It pains me to say this...but I'm over the everyone is in love with Nora complex. I simply love the girl to death, but to me, she took it too far in this one. <br><br>Zach, Wesley, Søren, Daniel, Griffin, Michael, Wyatt...and now this new person. I'm over it. I don't love her any less, but come on! This was a story about her and Søren (finally!), and although I like that it was told to who it was told to, it felt tainted to me. I know Søren is okay with her sleeping around, but to me...this new person should have been a hard limit. It's stupid to say, but I lost a little respect for her. <br><br>Basically I am a little pissed off that this new person is smitten with her within no time at all. Too many men are falling at her feet. At first I thought this was pretty kick ass, but now it's just to much. It overshadowed the awesome and unconventional love story that I've been waiting for. Maybe this is why I'm starting to fall more and more for Kingsley...he's not caught in the Nora web. <br><br>Ok, rant done!  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_603615005" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/603615005" />
    <a title="TeriLyn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1459307-terilyn"><img alt="TeriLyn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1396453806p2/1459307.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/603615005?book_show_action=true">Apr 30, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="TeriLyn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="TeriLyn" href="/user/show/1459307-terilyn">TeriLyn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1459307-terilyn?shelf=re-reads">re-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1459307-terilyn?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1459307-terilyn?shelf=2014-favorites">2014-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1459307-terilyn?shelf=ultimate-favorites">ultimate-favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer603615005" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18276124015111123936">**<i>The Saint</i> generously provided by Harlequin via NetGalley in exchange for an honest review.**<br/><br/><b>5+++ Forever & Everything Stars</b><br/><br/><i>"Once there lived..."</i> <br/><br/>I'd rate this 100 stars if GR would give me the option.<br/><br/><i>"The story starts with a stick and ends with an orgy..."</i> <br/><br/>Tiffany Reisz. Good god (I haven’t decided if the pun is intended or not), the woman writes a powerful, gripping story. She’s tricky that Tiffany. I felt like an anxious, young child on the edge of my seat at story time willing Wilbur’s surv</span>
  <span id="freeText18276124015111123936" style="display:none">**<i>The Saint</i> generously provided by Harlequin via NetGalley in exchange for an honest review.**<br /><br /><b>5+++ Forever &amp; Everything Stars</b><br /><br /><i>"Once there lived..."</i> <br /><br />I'd rate this 100 stars if GR would give me the option.<br /><br /><i>"The story starts with a stick and ends with an orgy..."</i> <br /><br />Tiffany Reisz. Good god (I haven’t decided if the pun is intended or not), the woman writes a powerful, gripping story. She’s tricky that Tiffany. I felt like an anxious, young child on the edge of my seat at story time willing Wilbur’s survival in Charlotte’s Web. Then I finished and Sting keeps singing in my head "Every little thing she is does magic. Everything she do just turns me on” - two lines in a chorus accurately reflecting this author. <br /><br />In my review for <i>The Mistress</i> I called Ms. Reisz a mad scientist with words – I’m holding to that notion and adding magician. The magic of her writing so precise, always giving just enough but never everything all at once, makes her method of storytelling agonizing to the point of addiction. You feel pain and pleasure; you’re turned on and intrigued by her dangerous and forbidden plots. She forces you to believe in her characters, to fall in love with them opening your mind causing you to think differently about two worlds, each so controversial and opposite, blended together through a journey of spiritual eroticism understanding how they’re a perfect match. Stories within stories all directly parallel to the central love story of the entire series. A formidable master of her craft, Tiffany Reisz presents brilliance with <i>The Saint</i>. <br /><br />The intricate plot is such that I can’t reveal too much or you’ll miss the magic entirely; the surprises of the plot thunder through you like a stampede and you welcome the trample. But know this – if you’ve read The Original Sinners Series (which if you haven’t please do) you’ll learn things you never even knew to expect. Mind bending truths changing the way you see everything. We get the beauty of going back in time reliving the treasure that embodies the beautiful beginning of a legendary, forbidden love. A young woman dredging through a murky river of life meets a man whose light shines on her like a lighthouse calling ships in from the storm. From the moment they meet a connection so strong draws them together; the start of decades full of love, humility, patience, danger, longing, and understanding. Every character we meet plays a crucial part to the story each of those characters just as captivating as Nora. <br /><br /><i>“You are one of my strengths, my greatest strength.”</i> Soren and Nora. This book seems like a dedication to them, to the world they’ve created, the launching pad for so many other great loves in their lives. It's a dedication to the sacrifices they've each made for each other. Their relationship epitomizes trust in its rawest form. The freedom in it feels transcendent. Like jumping off the highest peak in the world and learning you can fly. A belief in each other that runs so deep like the roots of a mighty oak tree keeping it alive for 100 years. The purity of their love is as true just as the sun rises and sets every day. It breaks you down and builds you back up. This is the stuff great fairy tales are made of. Lucky for us we get the added bonus of hot sex, danger, and debauchery. You want to be Nora. She’s the Cinderella of the kink world – of adult fairy tales - bold and incredibly brave, crass yet so refined, hilariously intelligent. We receive so much witty banter from these two it’s like really good foreplay building until we finally get to the point of no return. You want to be Nora because above all else her prince - a tall, arrogant, brilliant blonde god - makes dreams come true. <br /><br />Tiffany Reisz constantly reminds us why we love The Original Sinners. Her books excite us and remind us also why we love to read; the intelligence and thoughtfulness bleeding from the pages seeps into our souls and roots there. I get an education every time I read a Reisz story. I’m captivated, hooked - forever a fan. I’m simply fascinated. I know I recommend a lot of books. I read a lot of books. I love a lot of books dearly. But these books are my favorite by a long shot. If you’re an erotica lover and haven’t read this series you’re doing yourself a great disservice. It's egdy and sexy and utterly consuming. Because like any great magician, Tiffany Reisz pulls off her magic trick masterfully leaving the audience wondering how in the hell she did it again so brilliantly, reeling for more, thinking about her story far beyond when you read the end. Soren, fascinated by Nora after one of her particularly witty remarks, states <i>“your mind must be the most marvelous playground”</i> – I’m projecting the same sentiment to Ms. Reisz. <br /><br /><br />Favorite Quotes:<br /><i>“When you aren’t trying to look beautiful, you look beautiful. When you are trying to look beautiful, you are stunning.” “I hate you.”<br /><br />“The tears came in silent waves as inside the privacy of her own mind, she burned her dreams to ashes. What would rise from those ashes she didn’t know – she only knew something would be born from them, something she’d never seen before. A new dream. A better dream.” <br /><br />“If God looked like Soren there would be no atheists.”</i><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><b><i>The Saint</i> releases 6/24/14.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="18276124015111123936" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_444322953" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/444322953" />
    <a title="Stacia (the 2010 club)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club"><img alt="Stacia (the 2010 club)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1417661051p2/4013351.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/444322953?book_show_action=true">Oct 29, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stacia (the 2010 club)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stacia (the 2010 club)" href="/user/show/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club">Stacia (the 2010 club)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Someone looking for dark, edgy, and contemplative eroticism.</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=lgbtq">lgbtq</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=menage">menage</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=bdsm-or-person-in-control">bdsm-or-person-in-control</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=contemporary-romance">contemporary-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=frustrating">frustrating</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=favorite-book-guys">favorite-book-guys</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=romantica-or-erotica">romantica-or-erotica</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=dark-or-taboo">dark-or-taboo</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=extremely-unique">extremely-unique</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer444322953" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9972991513865512445"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1408048069i/10801668.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>Did anyone else feel like they were stuck in a wacky episodic series as they were reading? Or was that just me? <br/><br/><b>Reviewer Note :</b> <i>The Saint</i> is part prequel and part continuation of the Original Series series. I would not start with this book if you are new to Reisz because you will have some things spoiled and you also might not understand some of the character backstory. A good jumping off point for the entire series would be to start with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10970532.The_Siren__The_Original_Sinners___1_' title='The Siren (The Original Sinners, #1) by Tiffany Reisz' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Siren</a>.<br/><br/><i>The Saint</i> gives an entirely new meaning to "tel</span>
  <span id="freeText9972991513865512445" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1408048069i/10801668.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Did anyone else feel like they were stuck in a wacky episodic series as they were reading? Or was that just me? <br><br><b>Reviewer Note :</b> <i>The Saint</i> is part prequel and part continuation of the Original Series series. I would not start with this book if you are new to Reisz because you will have some things spoiled and you also might not understand some of the character backstory. A good jumping off point for the entire series would be to start with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10970532.The_Siren__The_Original_Sinners___1_" title="The Siren (The Original Sinners, #1) by Tiffany Reisz" rel="nofollow noopener">The Siren</a>.<br><br><i>The Saint</i> gives an entirely new meaning to "tell me a bedtime story." Normally, when a person asks their current lover about previous lovers, they want to know the basic details of a person's existence. But hey, if Nico wants to know exactly how Nora got it from her multiple partners, who am I to judge? He's a braver (and much more patient - I would zone out after about 2 minutes of any person retelling a life flashback) person than I.<br><br><i>Mild spoilers ahead. You have been warned.</i><br><br>5 stars for Soren (when did I come over to the Soren dark side? Didn't I hate him at one point?). <br>5 stars for writing (for any flaws I may point out, this woman can write her ass off). <br>1 star for <i>yet another man</i> worshiping the ground Nora walks on (to the point of claiming extremely deep feelings). It's getting downright ridiculous by this point. <br><br>Rants first, then I'll swing back to what I loved. <br><br><b>Seriously.</b> I think I'd have a much easier time with Nora if she just engaged in tons of casual sex with multiple partners. THAT I could understand. I could even understand submissive worship. But for Nora to form a deep "love" connection with so many people in such an inorganic way (lots of strong and intensive emotion in so short a time) makes me want to kick things. <br><br>Polyamory is real (apparently, I'm spelling the word wrong because I'm getting spell-checked). It's something I've witnessed first hand with friends who live this lifestyle, but I won't go into all of that because I've discussed it before on other reviews. This series' all-consuming version of polyamory is a bit hard for me to digest. We all have the ability to love deep and form strong connections. Some of us have the ability to love multiple partners. But when you have multiple love interests (whether all at the same time, or in the conventional circumstance of leaving one person before finding another), you have multiple ways of falling. Maybe sometimes you fall slowly and quietly. Maybe the love is something that takes time to realize because the person was a friend. Maybe the person who fell isn't as ready to declare strong feelings for you right away. The only one of the bunch who seemed to have any real hesitancy or reservation about throwing his lot in with Nora was Wesley (and even that was less about holding back affection, and more about his conflicting feelings with her sexuality and polyamory). I'm not counting Soren making Nora wait because Soren was all in from day 1, whether or not they were having sex. <br><br>I could handle Nora meeting Soren and wanting to give him everything of herself. In fact, I loved, loved, LOVED the back story of Nora and Soren. I KNEW I would. We'd caught glimpses of young Nora before and I was much more enamored of young Nora than I am middle-aged Nora. I'm one of the few people who <i>doesn't</i> mind reading about insta-love or insta-connections if they're written well. And Reisz has the "writing well" part down solid. <br><br>So let's swing back to what makes me keep reading these books, since I am probably bound to bitch about Nora for every single installment. It is what it is. I don't like her and will probably never like her. BUT...<br><br>The sex is pro. This is how mediocre erotica writers wish they could write. Other than my hatred for the overuse of the word clitoris (the rest of the world says clit), the sex is phenomenal. It is shocking, brutal, sensual, raw, dark, and artistic as hell. Yes, this is true literary porn. <br><br>The scenarios are designed to push you out of your comfort zone. If you haven't read this author before, you're in for a few jaw dropping moments. After a brief adjustment period, you'll learn to look forward to these moments. <br><br>Reisz is FUNNY AS HELL. The sarcasm, wit, and dry humor just keeps coming. Who knew that you could be turned on one moment, disgusted the next, and then laughing the next? I have pages of highlights in my book from scenes which had me giggling in bed. <br><br>The amount of (non fluff) reflection of spiritual theology is brilliantly handled. I'm not a bible pro, but I know parts of it well. The fact that there's real discussion of the scripture in a dark erotic book is so strangely bizarre - yet it works in the most unique way. This part of the story adds to the depth of character that is Soren (and Nora herself - for all of my ranting, she is whip smart). <br><br>There's something to these books which make them stand out from the standard erotic fare. You won't find cookie cutter writing, which is reason enough for me to keep reading. The hot sex is just a bonus.<br><br>For good, bad, or even worse, I'm still riding the OS train. And so far, it's been one hell of a ride. I can't wait to see where the next book takes me. <br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="9972991513865512445" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/549368112" />
    <a title="Allison ❤️Will Never Conquer Her TBR❤️" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9080319-allison-will-never-conquer-her-tbr"><img alt="Allison ❤️Will Never Conquer Her TBR❤️" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1465384674p2/9080319.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Allison ❤️Will Never Conquer Her TBR❤️" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Allison ❤️Will Never Conquer Her TBR❤️" href="/user/show/9080319-allison-will-never-conquer-her-tbr">Allison ❤️Will Never Conquer Her TBR❤️</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/19311457-the-saint">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9080319-allison-will-never-conquer-her-tbr?shelf=best-of-2014">best-of-2014</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer549368112" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6866951159449358803"><br/><br/><a href='http://s1320.photobucket.com/albums/u538/allipalk/Gifs%20from%20AE/?action=view&current=A5A9BAFB-E724-4457-97DA-E19FD8F32231_zpshq4jp4py.gif' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1392469487ra/8565846.gif' alt='Photobucket Pictures, Images and Photos' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/><br/>Wow. Just wow. I find writing reviews for Tiffany Reisz books are very difficult for me. I think the books in general are so deep and emotionally consuming, anything I can come up with seems elementary and just...paltry. <br/><br/><br/><br/><a href='http://s1320.photobucket.com/albums/u538/allipalk/Gifs%20from%20AE/?action=view&current=9C50AC7C-D1D2-43FB-89B8-F9C9AEB96C05_zpsw8aagst1.gif' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1390665226ra/8259380.gif' alt='Photobucket Pictures, Images and Photos' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/><br/><b><br/>The Saint </b>begins with Nora taking some time away in the Black Forest. She's clearly grieving but we don't know why. Kingsley's son, Nico comes to visit and Nora finds herself telling him "her story."<br/><br/><br/><br/><a href='http://s1320.photobucket.com/albums/u538/allipalk/Used%20in%20review/?action=view&current=3b3035192e668dcd46ce1ca040a550ea_zpsc614ef04.jpg' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1401934313i/9870890._SY540_.jpg' alt='Photobucket Pictures, Images and Photos' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/><br/><br/>The Saint is alternating between the past and present as she tells N</span>
  <span id="freeText6866951159449358803" style="display:none"><br><br><a href="http://s1320.photobucket.com/albums/u538/allipalk/Gifs%20from%20AE/?action=view&amp;current=A5A9BAFB-E724-4457-97DA-E19FD8F32231_zpshq4jp4py.gif" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1392469487ra/8565846.gif" alt="Photobucket Pictures, Images and Photos" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br>Wow. Just wow. I find writing reviews for Tiffany Reisz books are very difficult for me. I think the books in general are so deep and emotionally consuming, anything I can come up with seems elementary and just...paltry. <br><br><br><br><a href="http://s1320.photobucket.com/albums/u538/allipalk/Gifs%20from%20AE/?action=view&amp;current=9C50AC7C-D1D2-43FB-89B8-F9C9AEB96C05_zpsw8aagst1.gif" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1390665226ra/8259380.gif" alt="Photobucket Pictures, Images and Photos" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br><b><br>The Saint </b>begins with Nora taking some time away in the Black Forest. She's clearly grieving but we don't know why. Kingsley's son, Nico comes to visit and Nora finds herself telling him "her story."<br><br><br><br><a href="http://s1320.photobucket.com/albums/u538/allipalk/Used%20in%20review/?action=view&amp;current=3b3035192e668dcd46ce1ca040a550ea_zpsc614ef04.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1401934313i/9870890._SY540_.jpg" alt="Photobucket Pictures, Images and Photos" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br><br>The Saint is alternating between the past and present as she tells Nico how she meets Soren...and eventually Kingsley. At first I was thinking to myself, "<i>This is their prologue. Why didn't we get this before The Siren?" </i> But after reading it, I totally get it.<br><br><br>When Soren and Eleanor met, I instantly fell in love with their unusual chemistry. Her teenager banter, to a priest nonetheless, was shocking and endearing at the same time. Instead of being put-off, Soren is clearly enthralled...he didn't stand a chance. <br><br><br><br><b>"Your mind must be the most marvelous playground."</b><br><br><br><br>Those first few months of their...friendship...relationship...were perfectly presented. Eleanor was a troubled kid and Soren felt it the minute he set eyes on her. She not only needed him, but him, her. This was not about the sexual...this was about fate...about destiny. <br><br><br>Soren and Eleanor have a forbidden love story of epic proportions. I've gone from a bit of shock to their taboo relationship to totally in love with their D/s love story. Watching Eleanor grow from a fifteen-year old snarky schoolgirl to Soren's deepest submissive and lover was such an evolution...nothing rushed, perfectly evolving both physically and emotionally. <br><br><br><a href="http://s1320.photobucket.com/albums/u538/allipalk/Used%20in%20review/?action=view&amp;current=da80425ee254d6253da8c120503d0680_zpsa8c06999.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380395981i/763009._SY540_.jpg" alt="Photobucket Pictures, Images and Photos" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br><br><b> "Mom asked me once what it would take for me to believe in God. I told her if I could meet one person who seemed like he was created in God's image, I would start believing. And then you."</b><br><br><br><br>The Original Sinners, I do believe is one of my top three series of all time. It's gritty, shocking and spellbindingly perfect. With each book, I delve into their story and don't come up for air until it's complete. And even after it's over, I find myself wishing for more....I admit it, I'm a total Soren whore. There, I said it. <br><br><br><br><a href="http://s1320.photobucket.com/albums/u538/allipalk/Gifs%20from%20AE/?action=view&amp;current=more_zps08554b15.gif" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380395820ra/762500.gif" alt="Photobucket Pictures, Images and Photos" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br><b><br>“If God looked like Soren there would be no atheists.”</b><br><br><br>Amen! Hallelujah! <br><br><br><br>As a loosely practicing Catholic, I was amazed how much I learned of my religion in general. Sometimes it was joked about, other times spoken with deep reverence. I felt like I learned something from this book I didn't already know from years of religious education and weekly Mass. Ms Reisz truly has done her research. <br><br><br>Looking forward to <b>The King</b>...Kingsley's early years!<br><br><br><a href="http://s1320.photobucket.com/albums/u538/allipalk/Used%20in%20review/?action=view&amp;current=9622b6bffd1b92eb36d50fa6da3e67e7_zps3ab1da2d.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380395820i/762505._SY540_.jpg" alt="Photobucket Pictures, Images and Photos" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>The Saint</b> is live June 24, 2014<br><br><br>And I thank you!<br><br><br><a href="http://s1320.photobucket.com/albums/u538/allipalk/Blowing%20Kisses/?action=view&amp;current=51550305-C0D0-4B2A-B6F3-1E764EC8C3C1_zpsipehpqkz.gif" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1394341543ra/8839883.gif" alt="Photobucket Pictures, Images and Photos" class="gr-hostedUserImg">

  <span id="freeText4677399360420812689" style="display:none">This was the 5th book of Original Sinners series and so far I'm really, really enjoying them very much. And I must say this story gets better and better with each book.... 😏Anyway I can't wait to read other books and novellas too. 😀😀😀<br><br>Søren, you own me body&amp;soul. I love you,sir. ❤❤❤<br><br><b>
  <i>He started to speak but not in English. It was Danish, his first language. She knew some Danish, enough for her and Søren to tell each other “I need you, I want you” without anyone understanding them. But in her fevered state she could recognize nothing he said, not at first. He murmured the words like a prayer. She raised her head and pressed a kiss against his throat, her most favorite part of his body, the part hidden by his collar. The final words of his prayer she understood.<br><br>Jeg elsker dig.<br>I love you.<br><br>“I love you,” he said, in his first language, and the words rose like a banner over the bed.</i>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('L6arDr72ih+QQg1L7foStB6PioEEPlm6yAoeM3TLiT6V0pQ3hM97CnluF/p1Ci2q7skDNhwpyrjR8BUm/DErXw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('yhobO+tj8vp+GNyM9JT/AvXqimYy7xIwjrNXiDUJ1qZwbiQC0VoD75c0xj1sZMAcBawD0Sr4gTKXSVydvfN0xw==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer6192040872848702344">Tiffany Reisz is the <i>USA Today</i>-bestselling author of the Romance Writers of America RITA®-winning Original Sinners series from Harlequin's Mira Books.<br/><br/>Born in Owensboro, Kentucky, Tiffany graduated from Centre College with a B.A. in English. She began her writing career while a student at Wilmore, Kentucky's Asbury Theological Seminary. After leaving seminary to focus on her fiction, she wrote <i>The </i></span>
  <span id="freeText6192040872848702344" style="display:none">Tiffany Reisz is the <i>USA Today</i>-bestselling author of the Romance Writers of America RITA®-winning Original Sinners series from Harlequin's Mira Books.<br /><br />Born in Owensboro, Kentucky, Tiffany graduated from Centre College with a B.A. in English. She began her writing career while a student at Wilmore, Kentucky's Asbury Theological Seminary. After leaving seminary to focus on her fiction, she wrote <i>The Siren</i>, which has sold more than half a million copies worldwide. <br /><br />Tiffany also writes mainstream women's suspense fiction, including <i>The Bourbon Thief</i> (winner of the <i>RT Book Reviews</i> Seal of Excellence Award) and the RITA®-nominated <i>The Night Mark</i>.<br /><br />Her erotic fantasy <i>The Red</i>—self-published under the banner 8th Circle Press—was named an <i>NPR</i> Best Book of the Year and a Goodreads Best Romance of the Month. It also received a coveted starred review from <i>Library Journal</i>. <br /><br />Tiffany lives in Louisville, Kentucky with her husband, author Andrew Shaffer, and two cats. The cats are not writers. </span>

He sounded open to suggestion, which was good because she had a suggestion.<br /><br />"Everything."<br /><br />"Everything?" he repeated. "As in. . .?"<br /><br />"Every. Thing."
